## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic deformation laws and on temperature through thermal softening or thermally-activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at small strains)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined strain hardening and thermal effect)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with homologous temperature softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal activation with hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal dependence)
- Ramberg-Osgood inspired: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (linear + nonlinear strain terms)
- Zerilli-Armstrong type (BCC): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T + c2 * T * log(epsilon + c3)) (thermally-activated flow stress)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (quadratic hardening with linear thermal factor)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * (c2 - T)) (strain with Boltzmann-type temperature factor)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (shifted power-law with thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear-to-saturating strain response → Voce-type form: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermal softening of flow stress → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**m) or (c0 + c1*T) with negative c1, reflecting reduced dislocation barriers
- Strain hardening exponent less than 1 → Power-law epsilon**n with 0<n<1, characteristic of work hardening in metals
- Arrhenius-type temperature dependence → exp(-c/T) or exp(c*T), indicating thermally-activated dislocation motion (Peierls barrier crossing)
- Additive yield stress plus hardening → Constant + f(epsilon) structure, separating initial yield from strain-dependent hardening
- Product separability in strain and temperature → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), common in constitutive models assuming independent mechanisms
- Logarithmic strain rate / strain sensitivity → log(epsilon) terms appearing in flow stress, typical of viscoplastic or rate-dependent behavior
- Phase transition or anomaly at specific temperature → Non-monotonic temperature dependence, possibly requiring piecewise or peaked functions in T

= 3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 22.651)
= -0.2138*T*epsilon + 82.085*epsilon
```

The key components are:
1. `T*epsilon` term (linear in T and epsilon)
2. `epsilon` term (linear in epsilon)
3. `epsilon^0.4475 * exp(-6.616/T)` — a fractional power of epsilon times an Arrhenius-type exponential in T
4. `epsilon * exp(-(T-367.02)^2)` — epsilon times a Gaussian in T

**Candidates with `log(...)`** (9, 17, 24, 27, 39, 48, 49): log functions can't replicate either `exp(-c/T)` or `exp(-(T-c)^2)`.

```

The GT has these basis function components:
1. `T*epsilon` (linear in both)
2. `epsilon` (linear)
3. `epsilon^0.4475 * exp(-6.616/T)` (fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type exponential in T)
4. `epsilon * exp(-(T-367.02)^2)` (epsilon times Gaussian in T)

The key structural features are:
- A term with `exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius)
- A term with `exp(-(T-c)^2)` (Gaussian in T)
- Linear terms in `T*epsilon` and `epsilon`

Now let me check each candidate. The critical question is whether the candidate's basis functions can reproduce these four terms.
